<div id="review_2363566674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2363566674" />
    <a title="Monique" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1072826-monique"><img alt="Monique" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579399786p2/1072826.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2363566674?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monique" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monique" href="/user/show/1072826-monique">Monique</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072826-monique?shelf=readingrainbow-school-librarian-wor">readingrainbow-school-librarian-wor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2363566674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16391206553397503136">Steampunk—<br/><br/>Hmm heard it was a thing so I am trying to get into it for my readers..I have attempted a foray in this genre with Hugo Cabret, a large YA illustrated novel about clocks and gears and creating your own life and freedoms..This one is another Scholastic read and it is a long one, I mean it is almost four hundred page book (386) and entirely too much to really sustain kid readers..I had to try and finish it though as I stopped another book for being too complex and wanted to take my bias </span>
  <span id="freeText16391206553397503136" style="display:none">Steampunk—<br /><br />Hmm heard it was a thing so I am trying to get into it for my readers..I have attempted a foray in this genre with Hugo Cabret, a large YA illustrated novel about clocks and gears and creating your own life and freedoms..This one is another Scholastic read and it is a long one, I mean it is almost four hundred page book (386) and entirely too much to really sustain kid readers..I had to try and finish it though as I stopped another book for being too complex and wanted to take my bias out and complete a thrilling adventure for my school library..(Side note: this was a rescue book from the Maryland Book Bank for absolutely free, ah love that I can fill my library without begging my school for money I know is hard to come by).<br />Alright so you get interchanging storylines from three kids in need of new lives:<br /><br />Giuseppe-an orphan who works for the evil Stephano who finds an abandoned green violin that plays amazing music and offers him a glimpse of making enough to be free<br /><br />Frederick-another orphan who is an apprentice clockmaker to an old man who demands a lot of him while he secretly works on making a clockwork man to astound the world.<br /><br />Hannah-perhaps my favorite character is also poor and in need of more in life; her father is struck ill and handicapped leaving her mother to take care of him without working and so to care for her parents, herself and two twin sisters she has to quit school and work as a hotel maid.<br /><br />These three unfortunate children meet somewhere on page 138 or so (their intro stories were entirely too long LOL) and they are introduced to Frederick’s clockwork man and the three plot to make this automaton come alive..<br />Sneaking into the museum the trio find a large bronze head and a piece of a golem which makes their large automaton animated and real around page 315—a lot of bonding and backstory happen but not a lot of action..As the book nears a close the three work on solving their problems together with Hannah receiving a better job with more money for her family and her father improving drastically; Frederick becoming the long hoped for Journeyman and creating more automatons after witnessing the noble and tragic death of his beloved clockwork man while saving his friend Giuseppe; and Giuseppe and his little friend Pietro also end up with their dreams of going back to Italy being fulfilled traveling with the rich Madame Pomeroy playing his green violin for royalty…<br />Overall this wasn’t a bad story, way too long and drawn out but engaging and different for serious readers to get into steampunk, automation, early 1900s, creativity and innovation to create a new future..walking, talking clockwork men..hmm maybe I will read more LOL……<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16391206553397503136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PWeIHV39RaypHc+WvcsJWJ8YHEUUWJ54XzixXxhrilbL4Sn/eZSJw/WjAmiQtAvHJCphnfwqyD1I66QRyuG4kg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sFJbaCH4Cp4qpW79zBdkV5ClbyA7PyLQmyzl35GIZOdG1PqKBZHG8XYbowPhaGbIK5cS+NNNdJWM//CRQwJWIw==')})
  }

Sara Brighton and her sons, Luke and Ammon, head west in a doomed attempt to reach Salt Lake City. Sam returns to the States in anticipation of a U. S. retaliatory strike, but finds his home abandoned, with no trace of his family there. In Chicago, Azadeh Pahlavi meets her adopted mother and little sister, who are enmeshed in their own crisis with life-or-death consequences. The end is near now.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"14445866727562902637\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16918266223583803757">Matthew Kirby was born in Utah, and grew up in Maryland, California, and Hawaii. As an undergraduate he majored in history, and then went on to pursue an M.S. in school psychology. For ten months out of the year he works with students, and during the rest of the year he writes. He and his wife currently live in northern Utah.<br/><br/></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/11337172-the-clockwork-three">Quotes from The Clockwork Three</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;He waved to the city and said good-bye.<br />The city responded by carrying on the way it always did, traffic moving forward uninterrupted, without slowing, as if it were trying to demonstrate its permanence and show him it would still be there if he ever wanted to return. That promise was the best and only thing he could ask of it.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/317543-he-waved-to-the-city-and-said-good-bye-the-city">17 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Giuseppe would miss them as well, but in a different way than he would miss the city. A city would stay the same. The same buildings. The same streets. Not forever, but for a great long while. But Frederick and Hannah would never again be the people they were right now, standing on the dock, wishing him farewell. Tomorrow they would wake up and be a little bit different and a little bit different the day after that, and in no time they might become people he did not recognize. Giuseppe knew it because they were already different from when he had first met them. He knew it because he was different from when they had first met him.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/317544-giuseppe-would-miss-them-as-well-but-in-a-different">17 likes</a>
            </nobr>
